< Review>
We were a group of 8 trying to find sitting at Cups Cafe on a Sunday. Our wait time was 1hr but the host was super nice and kept doing time checks with us and really did his best to seat us all together. Our waiting team was efficient and knowledgeable about the menu. The only problem I had was that I ordered the fish and chips and there was some plastic cooked into it. The manager was super helpful and even offered me something else to eat and helped to rectify the situation. That did not put a damper on our fun at all and I will definitely visit again, especially for the cinnamon swirl French toast!< /Review>

< text>
Let's be fair. Great atmosphere and honestly over the top customer service I have had nothing but smiles and multiple offers if I need anything I truly appreciate that thank you.

4 stars only because the gentleman that dropped of my food did not ask me if I need anything as I watch the tables next to me get that offer. No biggie I don't mind asking for hot sauce just by the time I got that then I notice no butter or jelly for my toast

I know I could have asked a second time and they would be happy I'm sure just don't like having to ask multiple times for basic things like that it makes me Feel I'm being over needy when I just want the standard hot sauce and butter for my toast that's all.

I still left 20% for my main waitress she did an excellent job as did the rest of the staff over all a good experience and felt the effort was there for me to have a wonderful breakfast and for that I thank you.</text>

<Date>1600032733576< /Date><rate>4<//rate><Review>This place is fantastic value.

We came here during COVID, while spending a week in Palm Desert. We were looking for a spot for a boozy Friday brunch and this was perfect!

I got the cups omelet, which was SUPER unique, with mushrooms, brie, apple, and cilantro. The omelet itself was pretty thick and felt like way more egg than was needed, but if you're looking for a filling brunch meal, this is definitely it. It was so much food, plus two pieces of toast, and that was with a said salad instead of potatoes. I can't imagine finishing this, or even coming close, with all of that.

For some reason the bottle of champagne was half price (no complaints!) so I got a whole bottle for $9, plus a glass of OJ to mix it with. It was great.

We had great service, our food was tasty, and we'd definitely come back!</Review>< Pictures>

Fortunately, I was lucky in googling and finding Fresno Locksmith Service. Ali, their representative, contacted me immediately via text (and this was late, after business hours by the way). < text>
This used to be my favorite restaurant in Sacramento, period.  I haven't been for a while and decided to order in.  What I got was a major disappointment.  The broth was flavorless, and barely enough to cover the noodles. The egg was hard boiled and unseasoned.  When I called to ask why it was different than I remembered, I was interrupted repeatedly by the person on the other end of the phone.
I even asked if they were under new ownership, it tasted so different. If I had been sitting in the restaurant and served what I had tonight, I would have sent it back and left.

Based on the interaction with the person on the phone and the lack of flavor in the food, I won't be back.<//text>

<Review>I had the shio. Let's start with the good stuff. I liked that they had the tare available for guests to add more flavor to their broth, and it was pretty nice. The noodles had a good texture and bite. Bad: The arugula and lettuce were weird and clashed with the dish. I ate them first so I could enjoy the rest. The egg was hard-boiled and not marinated and seemed really low effort and the chashu was not marinated either. The broth was not served hot, merely warm by ramen standards. The gyoza was served with sauce already poured over it and was excessively sweet for all of us. The salt for the edamame was very large-grained which gave it a very uneven distribution and we ended up with parts too salty and parts not salty enough. It was luke-warm. Can't recommend it based on the shio and tan tan and the worst ramen shop I ever went to. Tastes may vary.< /Review><date>1572240362518< /date><Rating>2<//Rating></record>

<text>Shoki Ramen, one of the original Ramen houses in Sacramento, is a local institution. While they may have changed locations, sizes, and prices over the years, the overly quality and delicious nature of the soup has remained a constant.

There are plenty of other places to get ramen in Sacramento but why look further when this classic is still serving up tasty noodles and soup in their convenient downtown location?

There can be a wait almost any time of year as it is very popular, so be prepared for that. I visited in January and there was approximately 20+ minutes wait to get a seat just for 2.

Typical price is about $9.90 for your choice of many different ramen dishes, and sides/appetizers run from $3-4 to $6-7 depending. They even have a small poke bowl for under $7!

Check it out for yourself and see what all the fuss is about, you won't be sad that you did üôÇ<//text>< Name>

< time>
1566308102813<//time>
<Gmap_id>0x809ad126d6879097:0x1e9f6dba6a88b67e< /Gmap_id>< Text>
Shoki has always been my favorite place for ramen in the Sacramento area. I've been coming to Shoki for many years and all throughout their numerous menu changes. While I can't say I've liked all the experiments they've done with the menu, I can say I've always enjoyed the broth of my go-to order: Kurogoma Tantan Men.

I typically order the Kurogoma Tantan Men (contains minced beef), but on my most recent visit I decided to try their newly added Vegetarian version of the item (Yasai Kurogoma Tantan Men).  I very much enjoyed this one as well!  Now I have something for when I feel like meat and something for when I want to go with veggies only. While the Kurogoma broth is not for everyone, I love the flavor of the black sesame seeds. They have many choices of ramen flavors, so if that doesn't sound appealing to you, give something else a try: shio (sea salt base), shoyu (soy sauce base), or curry (soy sauce base with curry sauce).

I know people who are partial to the less healthy ramen places, but I personally prefer the taste of the broth here compared to the numerous other ramen places that use MSG and unhealthy additives. I have always been in full support of the Owner's/Chef's passion for creating a healthier bowl of ramen, made from scratch and natural ingredients.

Even though they ignored my job application right when I graduated from high school, and I am reminded of that rejection every time I eat here to this very day, I return in spite of this because the ramen here is the best!< /Text>

Location is small, food is great and the staff is very friendly and helpful with any questions you have or recommendations you may be looking for. < username>
Tina Tsong< /username>
< Review>
We did not need to wait on a Saturday at 5:30pm, however it did start to get quite busy soonafter. The wait staff are friendly and attentive, which contributed to an additional star in my review. We ordered the Shio ramen and Kurogoma tantanmen, but I had only personally tried the Shio ramen, which I do not recommend. The dashi/broth tastes predominantly of katsuobushi (bonito) and really nothing much else; it is a light and very bland broth. Ironically there is not enough salt in the Shio (salt) ramen. The noodles are average, with a slightly more stiff chew. The boiled cabbage, which is unflavored, included a piece of the core which was unfortunate. I was disappointed that the egg is not the typical ramen egg with a golden runny yolk. This is a plain old boiled egg, which is cooked well but would be more suited for deviled eggs. The raw acrid spinach on top does not work well with ramen.  My significant other who had the kurogoma ramen commented that the minced beef topping was refrigerator cold. Their ramen fares significantly below average.<//Review>

<user_name>Alexander Scott</user_name>< time>
1534004593466< /time>
< rate>
2<//rate>
< review>
Shoki was my favorite ramen joint in Sacramento. That being said, the quality here has continually declined each year. At first I was happy to see all the new options on the menu for vegetarians, vegans, gluten intolerant, etc, but it seems that each time the menu is stretched wider, the quality goes lower and lower. Even the basics weren't done correctly (I don't remember ordering my noodles al dente to the point that the cross section is half uncooked). A marinated egg should be complimentary with a bowl of ramen, but even after paying extra for it, it was tough (old) and didn't have any flavor. Similar also to the cha shu which was thinly cut, dry, and had no flavor. The details weren't cared about as can be seen by cold meat on the tan tan men and the undercooked noodles. Also the service was quite bad. The restaurant was not even half full and there was a wait just to get a menu. If I wait to be seated then the menu should come quite quickly. Furthermore if I have ramen then I shouldn't need to ask for the condiments. Then after asking for them they didn't bring the chili oil which was why I asked in the first place.

Shoki used to be the best, back when they had fewer menu items all cooked perfectly but those days have ended it seems. I will miss you Shoki.<//review>

<Rating>3</Rating><Review>First off, I don't recommend coming here at night since the location is pretty sketchy.

This is a tiny ramen stand and once you're inside it's like a diner/ramen bar atmosphere.

I thought the ramen was just okay. I ordered a tonkotsu and it wasn't very flavorful. I ordered corn and they bowl was literally half corn. So I guess the ramen is pretty much however you choose to customize it. But the tonkotsu broth lacked a lot of flavor and my pork portions were small and not very good.

<Text>This is by far the best ramen place in Sacramento.  In fact, I'm confident enough to say that it's one of the top 5 ramen stores in all of California.  I've been to most of the best ramen stores in Los Angeles, the Peninsula, and San Francisco.  A few important tips.  Always get their tamago (boiled egg) with your ramen.  They cook it to perfection, and it has this delicate soy sauce flavor infused in them that makes them delicious and the star of the ramen bowl.  Their broth is deep, complex, but not overwhelmingly heavy.  It's actually pretty light.  Everything about their ramen bowl shows these guys really know what they're doing.  I would even go to this place if it was in Japan!  If you go there in the summer, also try their tomato ramen!<//Text>< gmap_id>
